- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Domain Lineage: Kubernetes Watch Event Delivery Path

## Your Task

Trace how a Kubernetes watch event is generated and delivered from etcd to a client application. Find: 1. In `etcd-io/etcd`: the Go file that defines the `watchStream` or `serverWatchStream` that sends events from the etcd MVCC store. 2. In `kubernetes/kubernetes`: the Go files under `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/` that implement the watch cache and event distribution (look for `Cacher` and `watchCache`). 3. In the kubernetes client-go ecosystem: the Go file that defines the `Reflector` that receives watch events on the client side. Report the repo, file path, and struct/type name for each hop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:

Perfect! I have successfully traced the complete Kubernetes watch event delivery path from etcd to client applications. 

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings on how Kubernetes watch events are generated and delivered:

### **Key Components Found:**

1. **etcd Source (Event Generation)**:
   - `server/mvcc/watcher.go` - `watchStream` struct that channels events from the MVCC store
   - `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/watch.go` - `serverWatchStream` struct that converts events to gRPC

2. **Kubernetes API Server (Caching Layer)**:
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` - `Cacher` struct that maintains a watch cache with an internal Reflector
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go` - `watchCache` struct that buffers and distributes events

3. **Client-Go (Client Reception)**:
   - `tools/cache/reflector.go` - `Reflector` struct that watches the API server and updates a local store

### **Event Flow:**
Events flow from etcd's MVCC store → gRPC transport → API server's watchCache → client-side Reflector → local application cache. This architecture enables efficient event distribution without overloading the backend storage.
